        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188362457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer708417129490408419">Loved this way, way more than I thought I would. Xcor exceeded my expectations as a character, to see him under Layla's unconditional love was fabulous! Loved Wrath, that's one badass mofo for sure and I can't not mention my man-angel Lassiter. I wanted more of him because ..... Lassiter!<br/><br/>Hated Qhuinn, really really hated how Ward has transformed him into a stroppy, hissy fitting little bitch. Maybe if Ward had pulled his character back earlier I might have warmed to him a bit but his "redemption</span>
  <span id="freeText708417129490408419" style="display:none">Loved this way, way more than I thought I would. Xcor exceeded my expectations as a character, to see him under Layla's unconditional love was fabulous! Loved Wrath, that's one badass mofo for sure and I can't not mention my man-angel Lassiter. I wanted more of him because ..... Lassiter!<br /><br />Hated Qhuinn, really really hated how Ward has transformed him into a stroppy, hissy fitting little bitch. Maybe if Ward had pulled his character back earlier I might have warmed to him a bit but his "redemption" came too late on in the book to be believable. Tohr sort of redeemed himself a little at the end but I still do not like the bloke, and hate the way he is with Autumn, that she always has to take second place. And don't even get me started on Vishous and his <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheating plans!! What the actual f&amp;ck??!!?? That totally makes a mockery of the whole bonded male/mate for life that's been spun throughout the series and the very last thing I want to read about in a paranormal romance is cheating, be it by thought or deed.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Please, please, PLEASE Ms Ward, STOP with the post HEA f&amp;ckery. Please!<br /><br />Despite my total hate on Qhuinn and dislike of both Tohr and Vishous and that blink and you miss it ending, this is still a 5 star read. Thankfully Xcor more than made up for Q, T &amp; V.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31282932-the-chosen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1781025780&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1781025780" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer615401153416443109">If you don't like SPOILERS, move along. <br/><br/>I originally gave this book a very generous 3 Stars. I'm still so mad about this book today (honestly, maybe even MORE mad!) that I downgraded to 2 Stars, but I'm seriously debating a 1 Star rating. <br/><br/>Random Thoughts:<br/>• Stupid, boring Xcor as a love interest. Blargh. He and the band of idiots are just BORING! <br/><br/>• And, with Xcor, suddenly, treason and attempting to assassinate the King is just, oh, NBD. I can smell you're a changed man, Xcor! Come the eff on! <br/><br/>• </span>
  <span id="freeText615401153416443109" style="display:none">If you don't like SPOILERS, move along. <br /><br />I originally gave this book a very generous 3 Stars. I'm still so mad about this book today (honestly, maybe even MORE mad!) that I downgraded to 2 Stars, but I'm seriously debating a 1 Star rating. <br /><br />Random Thoughts:<br />• Stupid, boring Xcor as a love interest. Blargh. He and the band of idiots are just BORING! <br /><br />• And, with Xcor, suddenly, treason and attempting to assassinate the King is just, oh, NBD. I can smell you're a changed man, Xcor! Come the eff on! <br /><br />• And don't even get me started on Layla just sitting back and taking all of the incredibly insulting, sexist bullshit which batshit crazy Qhuinn (who I used to like, but who can now be killed off for all I care!) and equally batshit crazy Tohr spewed at her until she FINALLY spoke up for herself just ever so slightly toward the end!! OMG, all of that made me FURIOUS! <br /><br />• Then there's Qhuinn going off the damn rails! SHOOTING AT THE MOTHER OF HIS KIDS...IN THE KIDS' ROOM!!!! Had I been Layla, I would have castrated that mothereffer!!!! <br /><br />• Then, POOF!! All of a sudden it's everyone friends and living together and happy-happy, joy-joy again! I mean, whaaaat?! Qhuinn should have been crawling over broken glass, begging Layla to forgive him!!!! That sorry sack of sh*t made me LIVID in this book!<br /><br />• Trez and Selena, Part II. No. Nope. No way.<br /><br />• V and Jane wouldn't keep having these ridiculous problems if V and Butch had been allowed to be together all those years ago as they were meant to be (probably with Marissa in there as well)! Because V and Jane do not belong together. Simple as that! JR Ward was a coward and didn't write what she actually saw back then, and that means we're always dealing with a relationship that doesn't fit - V and Jane. If your opinion is different on this point, keep it to yourself. I'm sick of hearing how much everyone loves V and Jane together!<br /><br />• This whole book and all of the threads were a mess! Inconsistent, poorly crafted, blah, blah, blah. What a huge disappointment!<br /><br />• Plus, I'm mad that after 12 years of reading faithfully, since randomly picking up Dark Lover in 2005, just after its release, and becoming obsessed with the series when I was reading very little PNR... I'm mad that I *know* I should probably let this series go, as I enjoy fewer and fewer of the books, and yet I keep letting myself get suckered into reading each book. Pfffffft. Whatever.<br /><br />• Finally, all of the 5 Star ratings on here are bizarre to me. Did we read the same book??</span>
  <a data-text-id="615401153416443109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605514448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer952854259098631392"><b>4 Stars!</b><br/><br/>To say I was excited about Xcor & Layla's story is an understatement. Ever since Xcor was introduced I have been drawn to his anti-hero, tortured persona, because I knew deep down he was a softie, especially when it came to Layla. Xcor blew me away in this book - he was so sweet and sacrificing. He realized his mistakes and tried to make amends in every way he could. His love for Layla was palpable, and overall he was just amazing.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456578.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Layla really proved herself in this story. She always cam</span>
  <span id="freeText952854259098631392" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars!</b><br><br>To say I was excited about Xcor &amp; Layla's story is an understatement. Ever since Xcor was introduced I have been drawn to his anti-hero, tortured persona, because I knew deep down he was a softie, especially when it came to Layla. Xcor blew me away in this book - he was so sweet and sacrificing. He realized his mistakes and tried to make amends in every way he could. His love for Layla was palpable, and overall he was just amazing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456578.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Layla really proved herself in this story. She always came across quiet meek and compliant. However she showed how fiercly she protects those she loves. She did not stand by and let those around her dictate who she can love and tell how how she is allowed to feel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456579.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Qhuinn really disappointed me.. I truly tried to sympathize with his feelings but his asshole behavior was too much. He was such an inconsiderate jerk! Like honestly who treats the mother of their children like that? Plus his resentment toward Lyric... and how he treated Blay?! Like it was just too much :(<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456580.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And do not even get me stated on V and Jane... I am so nervous. Those two have already been through so much!!! WHY J.R. WARD?! WHY?!<br><br>Overall I loved this. My main complaint is that I wanted more Xcor and Layla time. Obviously anyone who has read this series knows that the POVs jump all the time but I wanted a bit more attention on The Chosen Layla and the Band of Bastards leader Xcor.<br><br>BTW I watched an interview and J.R. Ward pronounces Xcor like <i>Core</i> but in by head I'm always saying it like <i>Score</i>...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456582.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The next book is Assail and Sola!! So stoked! I was actually hoping they would be next... Marisol and Assail have always been in the back of my mind since their separation... Now I just need to be patient for a year!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491873588ra/22456583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

Maybe you can make me love them. If you can't, no one can.<br/>Anyway, it's a new BDB book!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726228.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I just...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726229.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText18320241719940124609" style="display:none"><br>THE CHOSEN!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403538414ra/10105391.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I totally saw that title coming!<br>First of all...<br>...Layla...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726225.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384638562ra/6922440.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Xcor...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726226.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>...but...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726227.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'm counting on you, WARDen! Maybe you can make me love them. If you can't, no one can.<br>Anyway, it's a new BDB book!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726228.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I just...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460318844ra/18726229.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_1605972281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1605972281" />
    <a title="River " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34852389-river"><img alt="River " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487674730p2/34852389.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1605972281?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="River " class="user" itemprop="url" name="River " href="/user/show/34852389-river">River </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34852389-river?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605972281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13429173825124516858">After some thinking and re reading some things I sadly decided to take one star from this review.. I am a sucker for a good HEA but I can't with this book. <br/><br/><br/>Original Review:<br/>I have a lot to say about this book, I'm going to divide my review in couples/characters because it's just too much. <br/><br/><br/>Layla and Xcor<br/>I think almost everyone was waiting for this story, whether you like the characters or you just wanted to be done with them we were waiting for years and it was very satisfying. <br/>Xcor stole my heart</span>
  <span id="freeText13429173825124516858" style="display:none">After some thinking and re reading some things I sadly decided to take one star from this review.. I am a sucker for a good HEA but I can't with this book. <br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br />I have a lot to say about this book, I'm going to divide my review in couples/characters because it's just too much. <br /><br /><br />Layla and Xcor<br />I think almost everyone was waiting for this story, whether you like the characters or you just wanted to be done with them we were waiting for years and it was very satisfying. <br />Xcor stole my heart, he was not good guy but he was a character that suffered a lot in his life and that hardened him. <br />I like the development he went through in the series but I'm not sure in this book, i liked him but i did felt he was very subdued here, i didn't expected him to be fighting everyone but he was too calm for i what expected of him. <br />Layla was surprisingly likeable here, don't get me wrong she's never going to be my girl because I dislike her with everything in my heart but she was presented as a strong mother and woman, what I didn't like is what was done to make her likeable, more on that later. <br />As a couple they worked, the ending was a bit too perfect but I am a sucker for a HEA so, you go boy, go have your happy life. <br /><br /><br />The BB <br />The bastards proved they are great warriors and their loyalty to Xcor warmed me, I can't wait to see them kick some ass in the future.<br /><br /><br />Quinn and Blay<br />These are my boys, they turned me into an MM reader so imagine my excitement when I read their POVs, I was like hell yeah finally some quality time with Quay and their love, well jokes on me. <br />What I said before that happened to make Layla likeable? Well Quinn was a total and complete asshole throughout the whole book, he was an asshole to Blay, Layla, the King, the Queen and even his precious little baby! I wanted to throttle him. And that just pissed me off because really? When are we going to get just quality time with Quay? They deserve it, we deserve it JR!!! <br />In the end everything was good of course but that whole thing left a bad taste in my mouth, Blay is a perfect guy of course and I love him more than ever. <br /><br /><br />Tohr<br />I suffered with torhment because poor guy was a mess inside, he had a lot of pain inside and he didn't really knew how to handle it.<br />I did liked his scene with autumn but I would've love to see more because wellsie was way more present, and even if understand his pain and that he's never to forget wellsie I hate feeling like autumn is an afterthought. <br /><br /><br />Throe<br />This bitch! Holy shit, I am so confused, scared and kinda impressed but disgusted with him, this guy is resourceful and cunning and crazy and i think now he's probably soulless, lol. <br />He had a fucking scary scene that triggered me because I have anxiety and one of my biggest fears is not been able to control my body or mind and that scene fucked with my head so bad but what would you know? Bitch got out of it and now he might have the power to destroy the brothers, for real. <br /><br /><br />Trez and his surprise <br />If you follow JR you already knew this was happening because she said it.<br />Trez's girl is back, well kinda. (I don't remember her name because I hated that book) is more of Darius/John situation but not really.. <br />I'm looking forward to see how this situation develops.<br /><br />The Scribe Virgin aka the oversexed angel<br />This was so good and so I'm looking forward to the brothers finding out, also I'm really curious about what crazy Lassiter has under his sleeve for the brothers. <br /><br />Assail<br />I had totally forgotten about him, he's only mentioned here. <br /><br /><br />Vishus and Jane<br />My heart is breaking for them.<br />I've seen a lot people saying that they want Butch/V but the relationship issues have nothing to do with the cop.<br />I don't know how is Butch relationship with Marissa but I wouldn't like them breaking up.<br />These guys are core of the series and I think is disrespectful to want them with someone that's not their shellan's.<br />I get that they have chemistry but it wouldn't feel right. <br />V and Jane do have issues and honestly that's on both of them, they are both making mistakes, it's like they are settled for eternity so they just stopped working in the relationship. <br />The next story needs to be them, because I need so many answers, whatever happens I just want them happy.<br />P.s V with Quinn's baby boy was the cutest, I melted.<br /><br /><br />Overall this was good, a good addition but even though the book was long as usual I did felt like something was missing, I can't pinpoint what it was but I was left wanting more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13429173825124516858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1605459485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1605459485" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1605459485?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=review-requests">review-requests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-go-rabid-over">books-i-go-rabid-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-paranormal-romance">genre-paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=series-black-dagger-brotherhood">series-black-dagger-brotherhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-jr-ward">author-jr-ward</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605459485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3200591458307132059"><a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2017/04/the-chosen-by-j-r-ward-2.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430489640i/14717740.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>WARNING: This review is packed full of spoilers. If you haven’t read THE CHOSEN and don’t want to be spoiled, skip it and come back to this later. You’ve been warned. If you’ve read it… we can’t wait to chat with you in the comments about how YOU feel.<br/><br/>What were your thoughts before reading THE CHOSEN?<br/><br/>Francesca: I was beyond excited because … it’s J.R. Ward. I wanted to see Xcor and Layla get their HEA but I was also looking forward to what would happen with the Band of Bastards and who else</span>
  <span id="freeText3200591458307132059" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2017/04/the-chosen-by-j-r-ward-2.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430489640i/14717740.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>WARNING: This review is packed full of spoilers. If you haven’t read THE CHOSEN and don’t want to be spoiled, skip it and come back to this later. You’ve been warned. If you’ve read it… we can’t wait to chat with you in the comments about how YOU feel.<br><br>What were your thoughts before reading THE CHOSEN?<br><br>Francesca: I was beyond excited because … it’s J.R. Ward. I wanted to see Xcor and Layla get their HEA but I was also looking forward to what would happen with the Band of Bastards and who else would be getting a side storyline hoping to see a glimpse of who the next book will be about.<br><br>Annie: I wasn’t really sure what my thoughts were because I try not to expect anything when it comes to a J.R. Ward book. She usually impresses me so I don’t worry too much. However, I was looking forward to see how she was going to redeem Xcor and how he and Layla would find happiness in the situation they were in.<br><br>Angela: I didn’t like Layla from the last few books, so I really wasn’t excited to read her story. However, like Annie said, Ward usually impresses so I wasn’t worried about it.<br><br>Suzanne: You know the Descartes quote ‘I think therefore I am’, well for me in the case of the The Chosen it’s: J.R. Ward is bringing out a book therefore I am so excited that much spontaneous singing and dancing ensues.<br><br>What did you think about Xcor and Layla’s romance? Did it live up to your expectations?<br><br>Francesca: Honestly, no. Although I found them to be sweet together, it was all a bit anticlimactic. Their romance was already developed before this book and there was nothing new to add to the tension in their relationship in this book. That is other than the fact that Xcor is a traitor and they have to figure out how they will be together in the end. But as a couple, and the whole love thing, that was already sort of set up. I don’t think they carried this book enough as the main romance. Xcor and Layla as characters were interesting and thank God for me liking them because that’s one thing that did keep me enjoying the story.<br><br>Annie: Yes and no. I was happy with the ending and am very pleased with how they were able to come together. But these two are definitely not my favorite couple in the series. I feel like so much of Layla’s story was written in other books in the series that she didn’t have the heavy impact I was expecting. I liked how she stood up for Xcor and how she showed a little bit of her backbone. But at the same time, I did feel like she should’ve also taken more responsibility for her children.<br><br>I think Xcor’s story was a little stronger. I didn’t expect him to be able to get away or expect the level of torture he endured growing up. I liked reading his backstory and felt that it definitely added another layer to his character. But I still don’t see him as a “hero”. I think out of the whole book only a handful of moments made me fall in love with him.<br><br>Angela: I have my reservations about their romance. It had its moments of good and bad I suppose, but overall it was okay. Like I said, I didn’t like Layla to start, but Xcor did manage to win my heart. His story was heartfelt; from his tortured past and his changed present. Yeah, I believed his changed heart.<br><br>Suzanne: I think Layla and Xcor’s romance had such a fantastic build up, which was part of the reason I was so excited. I have liked and sympathised with both characters since they were introduced into the series, so seeing them paired together was great news. However, in this particular book all the chemistry and tension that Ward had so expertly put together seemed to fall flat. I was glad that they got together, but rather than being a big expression of passion and emotion as I expected it was all very…nice. And nice is not something I ever expect to see from Ward it’s too flat and pedestrian, rather than an explosion of fireworks, it was like a balloon a few days after a party, slowly deflating and a little sad.<br><br>What are your thoughts on Qhuinn and Tohr’s actions in this book?<br><br>Francesca: I got a bit ragey and angry (or a lot, realistically). Starting off with Qhuinn because he was totally over the top. I was ok with him acting out a bit when he found out what Layla had been doing, but he took things way too far. Honestly, I found it out of character and just made me want to slap him. There was no need for him to act like a total idiot and I couldn’t grasp why Ward took it there. Tohr, I have two issues. Same as with Qhuinn, he acted way out of character by blowing out of proportion that hate towards Xcor but he was also acting like a total douche to Layla at one point and I just can’t see him treating a female like that. I was very disappointed in both of their behavior and I really don’t think Ward did the right thing with all that unnecessary drama. Now the second thing that pissed me off about Tohr is the whole Wellsie issue. I’m sick and tired of it. If he wasn’t going to be ok moving on with his life then he should’ve maybe stayed unmated and alone. It really bugs me that No One gets put in the second best place EVERY TIME with him. How can she feel like she’s loved when there’s always a shadow that pops up? I’m kind of over seeing that aspect.<br><br>Annie: I felt that these two were acting a little OTT, Qhuinn especially. While I can understand and believe that he would be upset with Layla and worry about his kids, there are some things that he does and says that are completely out of character. It almost felt like Ward amplified their reactions to create conflict in the story because Layla and Xcor’s story wouldn’t stand alone enough.<br><br>With Tohr, I didn’t expect him to get so upset. We all love Wellsie and miss her dearly, but it does feel like we are going over the same conflicts that were explored in other books already. All progress he made with Autumn seems to be pushed to the side and although I believe that he will always have a place for Wellsie in him, I wished he focused on Autumn more.<br><br>Angela: I could not get over how these two were acting. They acted hateful and disrespectful towards Layla and to other women in the house. I understand they both have their reasons but I thought it was still uncalled for. I was in awe of how they disrespected a Chosen and Wrath’s Shellan, Elizabeth. Seriously, from the previous books, they would not dare treat any of the women in that house that way. Tohr also treated his mate like his second choice. Left to the side until he’s done with his issues. I get his issues by the way; I loved Wels and would take her over Autumn any day. Nevertheless, I felt like she was just second choice. The worst part is that Tohr and Quinn were disrespectful to Wrath to the point of deliberately disobeying his orders. Honestly, I did not recognize these brothers. Everything they did was so out of character.<br><br>Suzanne: So, this is where all the explosion of passion came in. And it was ridiculous andstupid and idiotic and childish and dumb and lots of other very unflattering things. Tohr’s little meltdown I can live with and didn’t give much thought. But Qhuinn. At first I was a little thunderstruck. Who was this character that Ward had written into her book and when were we getting Qhuinn back? He has an extremely violent and unreasonable reaction to Layla and Xcor’s relationship. One that doesn’t make sense and frankly one that completely disgusted me. He accused Layla of treason and then commits treason himself, truely his actions boggled my mind. And then the end! I don’t want to give spoilers but it left me wondering what the hell was the point?<br><br>What did you think about V and Jane?<br><br>Francesca: This is probably what pissed me off the most about this book. First of all, just pick another Brother for once. I’m tired of always reading about V and his problems. I want to see more of Phury, Z, Rehv, John Matthew, not to mention that I want to read about Muhrder. But no, we have to keep listening to V’s “poor me” storylines. He got his book. Then he had a big storyline in his sister’s book. I’m done! I’ve had enough V. That being said, the actual problems in this book made me think less of him. He’s complaining that his mate isn’t spending as much time with him (and I’m being nice about how to word this because in private I would be saying something else about his complaints) and instead of communicating with her, or better yet, figuring out with the King how they can get more medical staff to help her out so she doesn’t have the weight of the whole Brotherhood and trainees on her shoulders, he chooses to go mope around with his woe is me routine and then thinks about cheating on his Shellan. This goes against everything I believe the Brothers and matings to stand for. I’m not sure how I even feel about the fact that he may go a bit farther than thinking but not fully cross a cheating line. I may still not be ok with that. And Ward can usually do anything she wants and I can understand it. Cheating (and thinking about cheating in my book is the same) is crossing a line that I may not recover from. Honestly, this made me lose respect and love in this series and I’m honestly not so excited about the next book as I would normally be because I don’t want to see what she’ll do with this issue. If it’s not handled in a way I’m satisfied with, I would drop the series. It’s that big of an issue.<br><br>Annie: I really hope V doesn’t get more page time. His storyline is too redundant and I hate to see the same things over and over again. Although I do believe that V and Jane still have their issues that they need to weed through, he’s had so much page time already that I really want someone new to focus on. What happened to Murhder? I would LOVE an update on Phury and Cormia as well. I don’t mind revisiting the original Brothers again, but I wish there was more of an even coverage that doesn’t focus on the same Brothers again and again. I felt like the decision to do this just made several steps backwards in terms of character development. Are we really going to do this all over again?<br><br>Angela: OMGsh, V was also annoying me. I did not get why he was so emotional. I couldn’t understand his issues. I’m not sure if he’s bored with his life and he needs extra attention from Jane or he’s just not happy with what he has. I really hope his issue doesn’t go further than it has in this book. It just doesn’t describe what a Brother’s true mating is about. Here’s the thing, the brothers are not just any other males. They are top of the crop in every way. Fierce, sexy, loving, romantic, yes, they may have their eff’d up issues but still they when it comes to their females; they are supposed to be loyal in every way. And all those traits are to be expected to be remain true. But if he screws around…mentally or physically, I don’t think I can forgive that.<br><br>Suzanne: V. At this point I am so freaking sick of V and all his bullshit. Qhuinn’s dumb-as-fuck actions I can forgive, but V? V got me so angry in this book! Jane deserves better, I know she isn’t Ward’s most popular character, but frankly I pity her being stuck with someone like V whose emotions swing more than a middle age couple on a swingers retreat. He is supposed to be a bonded male and yet his every action in this book goes against everything Ward has been telling us since Dark Lover. And it made me so angry, if he’s got an issue why doesn’t he just talk to his mate about it? But no, he just decides to sulk and brood in the dark like every vampire stereotype known to man. Frankly I think he needs to change his name to Edward.<br><br>What about Trez and Therese?<br><br>Francesca: Two words… TOO SOON.<br><br>Annie: I like Trez and I like Therese. And I think it’s really cute how they met, but yeah, TOO SOON. I think readers could get behind it much easier if it happened a lot later. At this point, it just felt like Ward killed Selena off just to bring her back. I don’t appreciate being played like that.<br><br>Angela: Oh, as much as I would like for it to be true, I do agree with Fran. It is too soon. If Ward didn’t’ do it for Tohr and Wels, then what should this be an exception? I am like Therese though. j/s.<br><br>Suzanne: Hmmm, mixed feelings. I’m happy, ‘cos damn I want Trez to be happy and I liked Tres (ha Trez and Tres) but I don’t know. It feels like a cop out. I was devastated after The Shadows, I genuinely felt like I was mourning, the whole storyline really got to me and I thought it was a brave thing to do. Then, seeing his grieve in this book I felt it all over again. Then Tres pops up, and I am happy because YES HEA! I don’t know, I will see how it all unfolds.<br><br>Who’s book are you most excited to read next?<br><br>Francesca: Honestly, like I said before, I’m not as excited about the next one. I’m interested in reading about Assail but I can’t get so excited about a book for a character that wasn’t even in this book!<br><br>Annie: I want a freaking Lassiter book, dammit! How much longer do I have to wait? And is Ward planning on writing about all the Band of Bastards? Does that mean I have to wait even longer for a Lassiter book?<br><br>Angela: No one in particular. I do want more of the brothers and this world in general. I want to know what’s going to happen with the Bastards, Lassiter, and when is Lash and Devina coming into the picture? Most of all, what in the world is happening with Throe.<br><br>Suzanne: Hmmm, who do I want next? I am interested in Qhuinn’s brother and what’s happening with him. And, as Ward seems to like rehashing original couples, I want to see Phury and Cormia! Of all the ones she has done, they are the ones who needs a book.<br><br>What are your final thoughts on THE CHOSEN?<br><br>Francesca: I could probably summarize this book in one sentence. What the fuck was that? While THE CHOSEN still has some of the things we come to expect from Ward, this was the worst book in the series. It’s not cohesive, didn’t flow, didn’t hold my interest (it took me 4 days to read it!!!) and honestly it pissed me off. At times I wondered if this was written by the same author because it didn’t have the signature “Ward feel” for me. No spark and no magic. And by the time we get to the end after there’s been crap thrown around all over the place in the story, everything is easily, quickly and neatly tied with a bow like nothing happened and everyone is one big happy family (all living under one roof). Just NO! There shouldn’t have been any Qhuinn/Xcor male bonding (to that extreme) in the end. Layla forgave him WAY too quickly. Why does everyone have to be related? And why does everyone have to live at the BDB Mansion?<br><br>Annie: This one wasn’t one of my favorites. There was too much OTT reactions and not enough development for the next book in the series. I wasn’t too keen on the first half of the book but I did enjoy the second half a lot more. Still, it’s not enough to make me give it more than 3 stars.<br><br>Angela: I think this is my least fave of the series. I felt like everyone was out of characters and found myself saying, “who are you?” to a couple of the characters. I found myself complaining to book buddies about scenes and characters instead of my usual swooning or texting my excitement. Rated this one at a 3.<br><br>Suzanne: Disappointing. Everyone was acting very strangely and very out of character, I almost felt like I was reading the wrong author, this did not read like a J.R. Ward book. She normally has the power to move me, not the power to provoke me into flinging my kindle across the room.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3200591458307132059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EDj5kaXgfTwafBI0GPauy2V7QvAESpoP1ouOfUfXl73gQqreEPl3x1rYcCzpiTBUvUmLQXsYKqheY2sBdKLvQg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oqQDBVPIHVmSrsMLnYLuEVuqUfYtZ8pivbLWhHgWHQ9S3lBK5tEXotIKoRNs/XCOg5iYR1I1esU1WjP4S2Nl8A==')})
  }

Bestselling author JR Ward’s The Shadows continues the current tendencies of modern vampire fiction as TrezLath and iAm,<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText975093121020178960\" style=\"display:none\">The Shadows: (Black Dagger Brotherhood, Book 13) by J. R. Ward | Summary &amp; Analysis  This is a Summary &amp; Analysis of The Shadows. Bestselling author JR Ward’s The Shadows continues the current tendencies of modern vampire fiction as TrezLath and iAm, as well as their friends and associates, stumble into and through romance. Their stumblings produce politically charged results that speak to the arcane bureaucracies associated with vampiric depictions since Rice and White Wolf and permit the kind of open violence to be expected of super-strong, long-lived, intelligent predators stalking the nights of a world not unlike that of readers.  J. R. Ward’s The Shadows, continues the Black Dagger Brotherhood series into its thirteenth volume. In its main storylines, TrezLath and iAm both find their ways into romances that manage to reinforce their fraternal bonds. The former seeks to escape a predetermined stud-duty in no small part because of his falling into a love he ultimately loses, which the latter unexpectedly finds himself in love with a lover initially promised to another. Several other plot threads seem to flow from earlier volumes and suggest future works in the series, both in terms of personal investment and of political intrigue.  This companion to The Shadows also includes the following: • Book Review • Story Setting Analysis of The Shadows • Story elements you may have missed as we decipher the novel • Details of Characters &amp; Key Character Analysis • Summary of the text, with some analytical comments interspersed • Thought Provoking /or Discussion Questions for both Readers &amp; Book Clubs • Discussion &amp; Analysis of Themes, Symbols… • And Much More!  This Analysis of The Shadows fills the gap, making you understand more while enhancing your reading experience.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"975093121020178960\" href=\"#\" But because Lassiter tells him he must learn to love another to free his former mate, Tohr knows they are all doomed.... Except then a female with a shadowed history begins to get through to him. Against the backdrop of the raging war with the lessers, and with a new clan of vampires vying for the Blind King’s throne, Tohr struggles between the buried past and a very hot, passion-filled future…but can his heart let go and set all of them free?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"585455602742974379\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n
